{"uri": "2024-07-431587408", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "04:45:56", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T04:45:56Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T04:27:59Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9921568632125854, "url": "https://www.register-herald.com/news/nation_world/trump-expected-to-turn-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens-exit/article_feda8c76-fb90-51a3-8c00-dd64e63d82bf.html", "title": "Trump expected to turn his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race", "body": "Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris\n\nCHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris.\n\nTrump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, where Trump is set to visit Saturday.\n\nWith Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly on security along the U.S.-Mexico border.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden had been the oldest nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to (AP) -- Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris. Trump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina. Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nCHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris.\n\nTrump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, where Trump is set to visit Saturday.\n\nWith Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly on security along the U.S.-Mexico border.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden had been the oldest nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at {"uri": "2024-07-432456259", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "18:31:23", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T18:31:23Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T18:20:22Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9607843160629272, "url": "https://www.wxow.com/news/minnesota-news/trump-is-expected-to-turn-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens/article_ca747e80-8b50-5c64-b257-d225c7c3a6bf.html", "title": "Trump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race", "body": "Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major political parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the Republican former president to direct his ire toward his likely new Democratic opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris\n\nCHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris.\n\nTrump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nWith Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly on security along the U.S.-Mexico border.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at (AP) -- Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris.\n\nTrump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nWith Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly on security along the U.S.-Mexico border.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nWith Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly on security along the U.S.-Mexico border.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.With Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"He has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.Trump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.Harris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"Voters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.Quietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.At 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.North Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.Mecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.This year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.Democrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.Biden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.With Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.Cooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.Trump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.Wednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.The Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nDonald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris.\n\nTrump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. {"uri": "2024-07-432653440", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "23:52:13", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T23:52:13Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T22:45:08Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9372549057006836, "url": "https://www.wxow.com/news/minnesota-news/trump-turns-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens-exit-from-2024/article_ca747e80-8b50-5c64-b257-d225c7c3a6bf.html", "title": "Trump turns his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race", "body": "CHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attack lines Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, who he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden 's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and called her \"crazy\" for her positions on abortion and on immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly.\n\nThe former president's stop in North Carolina shows he's concerned about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at {"uri": "8242015734", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "22:14:13", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T22:14:13Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T22:12:15Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.929411768913269, "url": "https://www.idahostatejournal.com/news/national/trump-is-expected-to-turn-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens/article_2c8af4bc-88c4-5347-9dc5-b53142bf6c05.html", "title": "Trump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race", "body": "CHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris.\n\nTrump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nWith Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at {"uri": "8242101350", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "23:55:33", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T23:55:33Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T23:54:36Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9176470637321472, "url": "https://wsvn.com/news/politics/trump-turns-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens-exit-from-2024-race/", "title": "Trump turns his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race - WSVN 7News | Miami News, Weather, Sports | Fort Lauderdale", "body": "CHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attack lines Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, who he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden 's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and called her \"crazy\" for her positions on abortion and on immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly.\n\nThe former president's stop in North Carolina shows he's concerned about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nAdvertisement\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nRelated Biden will make a case for his legacy - and for Harris to continue it - in his Oval Office address\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte - the state's biggest city - was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nAdvertisement\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term-limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nRelated Secret Service director steps down after Trump assassination attempt\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear - injured in the shooting - was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena\n\nCopy the Story Link Related Headlines Kamala (AP) -- Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attack lines Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, who he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden 's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and called her \"crazy\" for her positions on abortion and on immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly.\n\nThe former president's stop in North Carolina shows he's concerned about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack | All Of Our Podcasts\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at http://twitter.com/MegKinnardAP ___\n\nJill Colvin in New York contributed to this report.\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. {"uri": "8242122852", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "00:19:58", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T00:19:58Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T00:18:36Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9098039269447327, "url": "https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/world/us/us-election-donald-trump-targets-kamala-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens-exit-from-2024-race-calls-her-radical-left-lunatic/articleshow/112000705.cms", "title": "'Radical left lunatic ...': Donald Trump targets Kamala Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race - Times of India", "body": "Former President Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attacks Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, whom he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina, marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far-left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and criticized her positions on abortion and immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly.\n\nThe former president's stop in North Carolina signals his concern about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team aims for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting her role in leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books, stating he had only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee, and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that appears to be stoking interest among younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump campaigned heavily in North Carolina even as the Covid-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats have also been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did little to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again turn to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term-limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally is also the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman getting so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nAt TOI World Desk, our dedicated team of seasoned journalists and passionate writers tirelessly sifts through the vast tapestry of global events to bring you the latest news and diverse perspectives round the clock. With an unwavering commitment to accuracy, depth, and timeliness, we strive to keep you informed about the ever-evolving world, delivering a nuanced understanding of international affairs to our readers. {"uri": "8242141733", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "00:44:04", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T00:44:04Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T00:42:22Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9019607901573181, "url": "https://www.idahostatejournal.com/news/national/trump-turns-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens-exit-from-2024/article_2c8af4bc-88c4-5347-9dc5-b53142bf6c05.html", "title": "Trump turns his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race", "body": "CHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attack lines Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, whom he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden 's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and called her \"crazy\" for her positions on abortion and on immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly.\n\nHarris is expected to make abortion a key part of her campaign, looking to present herself to voters as someone who will fight against abortion restrictions. Earlier this week, she said she \"trusts women to make decisions about their own bodies.\"\n\nThe former president's stop in North Carolina shows he's concerned about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump also accused her of being just as responsible for Biden's policies at the U.S.-Mexico border, which saw illegal crossing arrests reach record highs at the end of 2023 and repeated his pledge to conduct mass deportations with the help of local police.\n\n\"Kamala's deadly destruction of America's borders is completely and totally disqualifying. She shouldn't be allowed to run for president with what she's done,\" Trump told supporters.\n\nTrump has hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at
