On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared onstage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris's record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris's name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lieutenant Governor Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to (AP) -- Donald Trump is holding his first public campaign rally since President Joe Biden dropped out of a 2024 matchup that both major parties had spent months preparing for, leaving the former president to direct his ire toward his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris.\n\nTrump is expected to turn his full focus on Harris as he stops Wednesday in North Carolina, a swing state that Trump has carried in the past, but Democrats have seen as pivotal. The former president's trip to the state shows he's still concerned about keeping it in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nWith Biden's abrupt departure from the presidential race and Harris edging closer and closer to officially being the Democrats' general election pick, Trump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president, whom he's characterized as \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nPeople are also reading... On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at http://twitter.com/MegKinnardAP\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. {"uri": "2024-07-432707710", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "01:48:38", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T01:48:38Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T01:23:14Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8549019694328308, "url": "https://www.kulr8.com/news/national/trump-turns-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens-exit-from-2024/article_95a7c2b9-3244-588b-af80-33804490732d.html", "title": "Trump turns his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race", "body": "CHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attack lines Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, whom he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden 's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee. The rally concluded minutes before Biden addressed the nation to explain he dropped his reelection bid to \"pass the torch\" to Harris, who is 22 years younger than him.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far-left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and said she was \"crazy\" for her positions on abortion and on immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly, a denigrating approach to the first Black woman and person of South Asian descent likely to lead a major party's presidential ticket.\n\nTrump's speech signaled the next stage for the campaign may be especially brutal and personal, even as some GOP leaders warned Republican allies not to use overtly racist and sexist attacks against Harris.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump also accused Harris of being just as responsible for Biden's policies at the U.S.-Mexico border, which saw illegal crossing arrests reach record highs at the end of 2023 and repeated his pledge to conduct mass deportations with the help of local police.\n\n\"Kamala's deadly destruction of America's borders is completely and totally disqualifying. She shouldn't be allowed to run for president with what she's done,\" Trump told supporters.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nHarris' campaign released a statement after Trump's speech describing it as \"unhinged, weird and rambling.\"\n\n\"Unity is over for Donald Trump,\" said campaign spokesperson Ammar Moussa, referring to unity pledges made during the Republican National Convention.\n\nHarris is expected to make abortion a key part of her campaign, looking to present herself to voters as someone who will fight against abortion restrictions. Earlier this week, she said she \"trusts women to make decisions about their own bodies.\"\n\nTrump has hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nTrump's stop in North Carolina shows he's concerned about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event was his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like one held Saturday in Grand Rapids, Michigan, was held in an indoor arena. Trump campaign spokesman Steven Cheung said it's \"to be determined\" if the campaign will no longer hold outdoor rallies due to security concerns.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nARTICLE CONTINUES BELOW ARTICLE CONTINUES BELOW\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\n___\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at (AP) -- Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attack lines Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, who he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden 's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and called her \"crazy\" for her positions on abortion and on immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly.\n\nPeople are also reading... National Ice Cream Day 2024: Get cool deals and freebies at Dairy Queen, Cold Stone and more HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: All Wolves now playing at West Ridge Kilgore remembered as \"larger than life\" trailblazer Bristol Casino records solid $14.35M month during June Housing complex rehab in Saltville wins $2.4 million state loan Campus keeps tradition strong This theater season brings friendship, camaraderie and nostalgia to the stage Only the name has changed; 'The Classic' expected to become bigger and better Southern Gap Outdoor Adventure Unveils New Entrance Sign Herald Courier receives awards from Tennessee Press Association HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Next man up part of high school football BRIEFS: VHSL to hold public forum at Abingdon on Wednesday; Top-15 finish for Adam Hooker (Lebanon) at State Open of Virginia PREP FOOTBALL: Marquee games await Northeast Tennessee teams Wise free clinics have come a long way in a quarter century Washington board updated on new cell phone directive\n\nThe former president's stop in North Carolina shows he's concerned about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe has blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump has also hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nVoters in Indiana haven't backed a Democratic presidential candidate in nearly 16 years. But Harris, a woman of Black and South Asian descent, was speaking to a group already excited by her historic status as the likely Democratic nominee and one that her campaign hopes can expand its coalition.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, home to Charlotte -- the state's biggest city -- was also the scene of Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, edging out Nikki Haley by fewer than 8 percentage points.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nWith Harris now poised to take his spot, she may again be turning to North Carolina for some political help: the state's Gov. Roy Cooper is among the Democrats that Harris' campaign is vetting for a possible pick as her vice presidential running mate.\n\nCooper is term limited and cannot seek reelection. The highly competitive race to replace him pits Democratic Attorney General Josh Stein against Republican Lt. Gov. Mark Robinson, a staunch Trump supporter who is North Carolina's first Black major party nominee for governor.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event is his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nWednesday's rally also is the first since the resignation of Secret Service director Kimberly Cheatle, who said she took \"full responsibility for the security lapse\" that led to a gunman being able to get so close to Trump at the outdoor event in Pennsylvania.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like the one over the weekend in Grand Rapids, Michigan, will be held in an indoor arena.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at http://twitter.com/MegKinnardAP ___\n\nJill Colvin in New York contributed to this report.\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. However, Harris, who proudly identifies as Black and South Asian, was speaking to an audience already excited by her historic potential as the likely Democratic nominee.\n\nHer campaign is banking on this group to help expand its coalition. Now, that mantle falls to the 78 year old Trump.\n\nHarris, at 59, has kicked off a campaign that seems to be sparking interest among younger voters, who could play a crucial role in determining the outcome of what's expected to be a tight general election.\n\nNorth Carolina, a state that Trump managed to secure in both his previous campaigns, was won by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, marking the tightest margin of any state Trump claimed. Despite the ongoing COVID-19 pandemic, Trump campaigned heavily in North Carolina, while Biden largely refrained from physical campaigning and did not personally visit the state in the final 16 days of the election.\n\nMecklenburg County, which houses Charlotte - the largest city in the state - also witnessed Trump's narrowest margin of victory in North Carolina's GOP primary, where he edged out Nikki Haley by less than eight percentage points. This year, Trump had intended to host his first rally since the commencement of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but the event was cancelled due to poor weather conditions.\n\nInstead, Trump called in from his private plane.\n\nThe Democrats have also been striving to secure North Carolina, a state where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 triumph, despite the recent dominance of the GOP. Following his heated June debate with Trump, Biden made an appearance at a campaign event in Raleigh.\n\nDespite showcasing a more assertive demeanour than at the debate, it did little to alleviate growing concerns within his party about his chances of reclaiming the White House. Harris is now poised to replace him, and she may look to North Carolina for political backing.\n\nTrump's Charlotte appearance marks his second campaign rally following the shocking assassination attempt on him at a Pennsylvania rally on July 13. After recovering, he graciously accepted the GOP's presidential nomination and gave a stirring speech at the Republican National Convention, all while visibly sporting bandages from the shooting incident.\n\nIn a dramatic development related to the security breach, Secret Service Director Kimberly Cheatle has stepped down. He endorsed Harris, and Democrats have lined up behind her. Harris took in record fundraising hauls and some polls have shown a tighter race between Harris and Trump.\n\n\"He quit because he was losing so badly in the polls,\" Trump said.\n\nIt was Trump's first event in North Carolina since he survived an assassination attempt this month in Pennsylvania. Nearly every speaker made reference to the incident, citing God's hand in preventing Trump from more serious injury. Trump sustained an ear injury during the incident, which occurred at a rural, open-air rally.\n\nAfter the incident, Trump and other Republicans signaled the experience would lead to a change in his temperament and calls for unity in the divided nation.\n\n\"I became nice,\" Trump said. He then asked the crowd: \"If you don't mind, I'm not going to be nice.\"\n\nTrump, who typically gives his political opponents derogatory nicknames, called Harris \"Lyin' Kamala\" over and over again.\n\nThe crowd loved it. Video criticizing Harris on immigration policies was playing before the speech as the crowd booed loudly.\n\nAbout 10,000 Trump supporters filled Bojangles Coliseum, including Daune Galbraith, who arrived at 8 a.m. -- 10 hours before Trump was scheduled to begin speaking -- for her first Trump rally.\n\n\"He's for the people,\" said Galbraith, who lives in Greensboro and said she is excited to vote for Trump a third time. \"He is going to take care of America. He is going to bring back the America I grew up loving.\"\n\nTrump defeated Hilary Clinton in 2016 before losing to Biden and Harris in 2020. With Harris' ascension to the top of the ticket, Democrats hope to turn the election into a referendum on Trump -- who has twice lost the popular vote -- rather than a debate about the ability of Biden to do the job for another four years.\n\n\"She is fighting to protect our democracy,\" Mark Jerrell, the vice chair of the Mecklenburg County Board of Commissioners, said during a press event Wednesday morning. \"She's fighting to strengthen America's position in the world. The stakes of this election couldn't be higher.\"\n\nDespite the burst of enthusiasm for Harris, some Trump supporters believe he will have no problem winning in November.\n\n\"Because what has she done?\" said Trump supporter Sheri McReynolds, who is from Wake Forest.\n\nSeveral Republican officials, officeholders and candidates delivered short speeches, previewing the attacks on Harris over immigration, border security and liberal positions during her time as U.S. Senator.\n\n\"She's a San Francisco liberal who wants to turn the whole country into San Francisco,\" said U.S. Rep. Richard Hudson, who is leading the Republican effort to keep the U.S. House of Representatives. \"... She is wrong for America.\"\n\nCongressional candidate Mark Harris delivered a prayer to begin the event around 4 p.m. North Carolina House Speaker Tim Moore, who is running for U.S. House, spoke and earned his biggest cheer when he endorsed a proposed constitutional amendment to ban non-citizens from voting in the state. The proposal would reaffirm an existing state constitutional provision.\n\nU.S. Rep. Dan Bishop, the Republican nominee for attorney general, and Republican National Committee chairman Michael Whatley, the former North Carolina Republican Party chairman, also spoke. Each took shots at Harris, who has quickly united the Democratic Party with an immense fundraising haul, hitting her over immigration. Whatley said the November election is about \"strength versus weakness.\"\n\nLt. Gov. Mark Robinson, who is typically a featured speaker at Trump rallies, wasn't part of the program. And when Trump encouraged the crowd to vote for North Carolina Republicans -- listing them by name -- Robinson, the GOP's gubernatorial candidate, wasn't mentioned.\n\nPolice and Secret Service personnel were visible nearly everywhere outside and inside of the site, not surprising given the assassination attempt in Pennsylvania earlier in the month. The head of the Secret Service resigned this week under pressure from lawmakers.\n\n\"As you move to an indoor site, it opens up a number of different vulnerabilities that you don't have,\" former U.S. Secret Service agent Paul Eckloff told WRAL. \"A farm field is a far more controlled environment with separate ingress and egress to protect the staff, press and VIP ease.\"\n\nBut, he added, an indoor venue like the Bojangles Coliseum is \"already designed for crowd control.\"\n\nTrump carried North Carolina twice -- including by less than 1.5% in 2020 -- and has been favored to do so again, even as Democrats have made frequent campaign stops across the state. Harris has visited the state seven times in 2024.\n\nDemocratic Gov. Roy Cooper, who won the state twice with Trump on the ballot, is among the top contenders to be Harris' vice-presidential choice. Trump picked U.S. Sen. JD Vance of Ohio to be his vice president. Trump didn't mention Cooper or any other potential Democratic vice presidential candidates.\n\nInstead, he focused his broadsides on Harris and, to a lesser degree, Biden. It was a typical Trump speech, veering off and on his teleprompter, infused with humor and hitting many familiar topics -- protecting women's sports from transgender competitors, crimes committed by undocumented immigrants, a riff on Hannibal Lecter, the fictional killer who eats his victims.\n\nTrump said Harris \"can't ever be trusted\" and that she \"brazenly\" lied about Biden's mental capacity.\n\nPerhaps trying to neutralize a political weakness, Trump defended his position on abortion -- seen by Democrats as a potential liability for Trump, who appointed three Supreme Court justices that voted to overturn the landmark Roe v. Wade ruling.\n\nHe told the crowd that he supports abortion rights in cases of rape, incest and when the life of the mother is in danger but added that people need to \"follow their heart\" on the issue. (Photo by Galen Bacharier/NC Newsline)\n\nCHARLOTTE -- Former President Donald Trump launched a volley of attacks on Vice President Kamala Harris in a speech on Wednesday, calling her \"stupid,\" a \"lunatic\" and \"ultra-liberal\" in his first campaign rally since her ascension as the all but certain Democratic nominee.\n\nAddressing several thousand supporters at a packed Bojangles Coliseum in Charlotte, Trump painted Harris as \"incompetent\" and \"radical,\" ticking through her voting record as a senator and declaring her the \"driving force\" of the Biden White House.\n\n\"For three and a half years, lyin' Kamala Harris has been the ultra-liberal driving force behind every single Biden catastrophe,\" Trump said.\n\nThroughout he and other speakers' remarks, almost every mention of the vice president prompted loud boos. And throughout his hour-plus speech, Trump repeatedly returned to her role in immigration policy -- at one point referring to a \"Kamala Harris border invasion.\"\n\nHe took aim at her background as a prosecutor and attorney general, declaring that she \"ruined San Francisco.\" And he scrutinized her policy stances on criminal justice and policing, while mocking contrasts her campaign has drawn between them.\n\n\"They get me to that position and then the campaign says 'I'm a prosecutor,' and I'm a convicted felon,\" Trump said, referencing his conviction in a New York criminal trial. \"I don't think people are going to buy it.\"\n\nEchoing an ad released by his campaign earlier this week, Trump branded the vice president \"the most liberal elected politician in American history,\" and the \"original Marxist.\" Both of these claims are demonstrably false.\n\n\"She makes Bernie look like a moderate,\" he said. \"(U.S. Sen.) Bernie Sanders, he's actually quite moderate by comparison.\"\n\nPrior to the Wednesday rally, Trump last visited North Carolina in late May. Harris, who swiftly coalesced support from Democrats in North Carolina and nationally in recent days after President Joe Biden announced his decision that he would not seek reelection, has visited twice in recent weeks with events in Greensboro and Fayetteville prior to becoming the all-but-certain nominee of her party.\n\nThe former president swiftly addressed Biden bowing out of the race, telling supporters that \"he quit.\"\n\n\"He was losing so badly in the polls and down by a lot, so he quit,\" Trump said. \"But really, what happened was the leaders of the Democrat Party did a very undemocratic move.\"\n\nAnd though Biden no longer tops the ticket for November, he was still the target of numerous criticisms from his 2020 opponent. Trump called him a \"fake liberal\" while contrasting him with Harris, and recalled a conversation in which Biden was called \"cognitively a degenerate.\"\n\n\"I wish him well, but I don't like him,\" Trump said. \"He's not a nice person. He's trying to put me in jail, why would I like him?\"\n\nThose who attended the rally and spoke to NC Newsline expressed confidence that Trump would emerge victorious in November, despite now facing a new opponent.\n\nJohn Yopp, a law enforcement officer and former candidate for sheriff from Jacksonville, North Carolina, called Biden's stepping aside for Harris \"totally undemocratic.\" And he equated the vice president's candidacy to the infamous \"New Coke\" marketing campaign.\n\n\"It got a lot of people's attention, but it was superficial, it disappeared quickly,\" Yopp said. \"That's what's going to happen here.\"\n\nAnother said he didn't believe Trump's chances of victory had changed despite Harris now leading the Democratic ticket.\n\n\"At the end of the day, her policies are Biden's policies,\" said Doyle Ball, who traveled from Tennessee to attend the Wednesday rally.\n\nAn array of Republicans that will appear on the ballot below Trump threw their support behind the nominee ahead of his speech Wednesday.\n\nMark Harris, who is running for Congress in North Carolina's 8th House District, led the coliseum in prayer. It was \"an act of God\" that prevented Trump from further injury during the assassination attempt in Pennsylvania, he said.\n\n\"It is by your grace and by your mercy and your hand that was upon President Trump that caused him to turn his head,\" Harris said.\n\nSpeaker of the House Tim Moore, also seeking a seat in Congress, touted the Republican-led legislature's priorities in recent years. And U.S. Rep. Dan Bishop, running for attorney general, sought to tie his Democratic opponent to Harris, calling them \"radical.\"\n\n\"The last thing North Carolina needs, and America needs, is more prosecutors like Jeff Jackson and Kamala Harris,\" Bishop said.\n\nHarris' campaign gathered local officials for a press conference ahead of the rally -- continuing to home in on abortion rights and Project 2025 as top lines of attack against Trump.\n\nThe wide-ranging conservative policy agenda from the Heritage Foundation has increasingly come into focus from Democrats, who say it is effectively a blueprint for Trump's second term in office. The former president has dismissed the plan and tried to distance himself from its authors and endorsers, a number of whom served in his administration.\n\n\"Donald Trump's Project 2025 threatens to roll back the rights and freedoms of the American people and give the presidency more power and less accountability than ever before,\" Mecklenburg County Commissioner Mark Jerrell said.\n\nThe campaign also featured Hadley Duvall, a sexual assault survivor and abortion rights advocate who featured in a prominent ad for Kentucky Gov. Andy Beshear's campaign.\n\n\"Donald Trump has come to North Carolina today to brag about how he overturned Roe v. Wade and ripped away reproductive freedom from women and girls across the country,\" Duvall said. \"He is proudly responsible for each and every one of the cruel abortion bans across the country, Harris, after being endorsed by Biden to run at the top of the Democratic ticket, in recent days has seen a bump in polling compared to Biden's lagging performance, including among independents, people of color and women, among other critical voting blocs.\n\n\"Now,\" said Bryson Davis, an 18-year-old from Statesville, \"he's running against somebody that's competent. \"Kamala is probably going to come off a little more fiery than Joe would.\"\n\nOr as Castillo put it, \"The fact she isn't suffering from old age ... it's definitely going to give her a huge bump right away. She can talk. She can laugh, obviously.\"\n\nFor the former president, Harris' ascension was but a new invitation to fight -- and the crowd ate it up. Look at her. She's beautiful. She's so magnificent.'\"\n\nTrump this week agreed to debate Harris, and said he would be \"willing to do more than one debate\" against her. Richard Hudson (R-N.C.), chair of the National Republican Congressional Committee, offering nearly identical criticism.\n\nWhat kind of attacks Republicans will consider in bounds is still a matter of uncertainty. But asked if taking that approach was off limits for Trump, Cheung said that it wasn't necessarily.\n\n\"I don't know it's off limits,\" he said. \"But it's not something that we've done. So it's not even on our radar.\"\n\nSimilarly, Michael Whatley, the chair of the Republican National Committee and former chair of the North Carolina Republican Party, in an interview declined to say whether he agreed with Johnson's remarks about staying away from Harris' race or gender -- instead, he said what he thought the party should focus on.\n\n\"Look, I think we need to talk about her being an extreme California liberal,\" Whatley said, criticizing policies she supported in her home state, in the Senate and as Biden's vice president.\n\nPressed again, Whatley said the Republican Party is \"going to focus all day, every day on the American voters,\" and telling them about Trump's policies.\n\nEven before Trump took the stage, the GOP's focus -- evident in speakers' remarks before him -- had dramatically moved away from Biden and onto Harris. {"uri": "8242271551", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "03:19:17", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T03:19:17Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T03:16:58Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8745098114013672, "url": "https://www.eagletribune.com/region/trump-turns-his-full-focus-on-harris-at-first-rally-since-bidens-exit-from-2024/article_5f451760-bc0c-594f-919c-f8131b490d71.html", "title": "Trump turns his full focus on Harris at first rally since Biden's exit from 2024 race", "body": "Republican presidential candidate former President Donald Trump speaks at a campaign rally in Charlotte, N.C., Wednesday, July 24, 2024.\n\nCHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Donald Trump unleashed a barrage of attack lines Wednesday against his likely new opponent, Vice President Kamala Harris, whom he called his \"new victim to defeat\" and accused of deceiving the public about President Joe Biden 's ability to run for a second term.\n\nThe rally in Charlotte, North Carolina marked his first public campaign event since Biden dropped out of the 2024 matchup and Harris became the Democrats' likely nominee. The rally concluded minutes before Biden addressed the nation to explain he dropped his reelection bid to \"pass the torch\" to Harris, who is 22 years younger than him.\n\n\"So now we have a new victim to defeat: Lyin' Kamala Harris,\" Trump said, labeling her \"the most incompetent and far-left vice president in American history.\"\n\nTrump called her a \"radical left lunatic\" and said she was \"crazy\" for her positions on abortion and on immigration. He also mispronounced her first name repeatedly, a denigrating approach to the first Black woman and person of South Asian descent likely to lead a major party's presidential ticket.\n\nTrump's speech signaled the next stage for the campaign may be especially brutal and personal, even as some GOP leaders warned Republican allies not to use overtly racist and sexist attacks against Harris.\n\nTrump has ramped up his criticism of the vice president since Biden's abrupt departure, calling Harris \"the same as Biden but much more radical.\"\n\nHe blamed her for what he portrays as the Biden administration's failures, particularly security along the U.S.-Mexico border. On Wednesday, the speakers who appeared on stage before the Republican nominee attacked Harris' record on the border, highlighting she was tasked with leading a White House effort to tackle migration issues. Harris' name was met with boos several times during the speeches.\n\n\"She was assigned that, she was given that task, and she failed,\" said Brandon Judd, former president of the National Border Patrol Council, the union that represents agents.\n\nTrump also accused Harris of being just as responsible for Biden's policies at the U.S.-Mexico border, which saw illegal crossing arrests reach record highs at the end of 2023 and repeated his pledge to conduct mass deportations with the help of local police.\n\n\"Kamala's deadly destruction of America's borders is completely and totally disqualifying. She shouldn't be allowed to run for president with what she's done,\" Trump told supporters.\n\nHarris, meanwhile, spent Wednesday in Indiana, telling members of the historically Black sorority Zeta Phi Beta that \"we are not playing around\" and asked for their help in electing her president in November, an election she characterized as \"a choice between two different visions for our nation, one focused on the future, the other focused on the past.\"\n\nHarris' campaign released a statement after Trump's speech describing it as \"unhinged, weird and rambling.\"\n\n\"Unity is over for Donald Trump,\" said campaign spokesperson Ammar Moussa, referring to unity pledges made during the Republican National Convention.\n\nHarris is expected to make abortion a key part of her campaign, looking to present herself to voters as someone who will fight against abortion restrictions. Earlier this week, she said she \"trusts women to make decisions about their own bodies.\"\n\nTrump has hedged on plans for an expected debate with Harris, first saying that he wanted Fox News, not ABC, to host the matchup he had originally scheduled for September with Biden. On Tuesday, Trump appeared to tweak that message again, saying on a call with reporters that he'd like to debate Harris \"more than once\" but not committing to appearing at the debate currently on the books and saying he'd only agreed to debate Biden twice, not Harris.\n\nQuietly, Republicans have spoken about how subbing Harris in for Biden nullifies a portion of their party's argument in favor of Trump's vitality and vigor.\n\nAt 81, Biden would have been the oldest presidential nominee heading into a general election. Now, the 78-year-old Trump occupies that slot. Harris, 59, has launched a campaign that at least in some corners appears to be stoking interest among the younger voters who could be key in deciding an anticipated close general election.\n\nTrump's stop in North Carolina shows he's concerned about keeping the state in his column this November, even as his team reaches for wins in traditionally Democratic-leaning states like Minnesota, which Trump is set to visit on Saturday.\n\nNorth Carolina is a state Trump carried in both his previous campaigns but by less than 1.5 percentage points over Biden in 2020, the closest margin of any state Trump won. Trump stumped heavily in North Carolina even as the COVID-19 pandemic wore on, while Biden largely kept off the physical campaign trail and did not personally visit the state in the last 16 days of the election.\n\nThis year, Trump had planned to hold his first rally since the start of his hush money trial in Fayetteville, but that event was called off due to inclement weather. Trump called in from his private plane instead.\n\nDemocrats also have been working to win North Carolina, where the party's most recent presidential win was Barack Obama's 2008 victory, despite recent GOP dominance.\n\nBiden held a campaign event in Raleigh the day after his disastrous June debate with Trump. While he was much more forceful in that appearance than he was on the debate stage, it did not help much to quell the growing concern from members of his party about his ability to win the White House again.\n\nTrump's Charlotte event was his second campaign rally since a July 13 assassination attempt at a Pennsylvania rally. Days later, Trump accepted the GOP presidential nomination and gave a speech at the Republican National Convention, where his ear -- injured in the shooting -- was bandaged.\n\nThe Charlotte rally, like one held Saturday in Grand Rapids, Michigan, was held in an indoor arena. Trump campaign spokesman Steven Cheung said it's \"to be determined\" if the campaign will no longer hold outdoor rallies due to security concerns.\n\nMeg Kinnard can be reached at
